<div id="review_551857616" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/551857616" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4844873-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299680097p2/4844873.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/551857616?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/4844873-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4844873-laura?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer551857616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11858876673395740303">**Caution Spoilers Ahead**<br/><br/><b>”a life without living was simply a death without dying”</b><br/><br/>All the whispers, rants and raves hopping around GR about Evenfall are true! The updates alone scared the bejesus out of me! Haha… I was shaking in my reading booties even before I made one kindle click. Just a few steps in though; my fear turned into a fierce, addictive love with gut twisting, heart breaking, pulse racing intensity. It terrifies me how fast this world, words, and characters got under my skin. NO O</span>
  <span id="freeText11858876673395740303" style="display:none">**Caution Spoilers Ahead**<br /><br /><b>”a life without living was simply a death without dying”</b><br /><br />All the whispers, rants and raves hopping around GR about Evenfall are true! The updates alone scared the bejesus out of me! Haha… I was shaking in my reading booties even before I made one kindle click. Just a few steps in though; my fear turned into a fierce, addictive love with gut twisting, heart breaking, pulse racing intensity. It terrifies me how fast this world, words, and characters got under my skin. NO ONE gets to me that fast in fiction or life. But let’s face it…my heart’s bitter, ironclad walls of denial, deflections, and sarcasm didn’t stand a chance against Hsin Liu Vega. <br /><br />Let me try to introduce the world of Evenfall though before this turns into a Hsin gush-fest. :) We are thrown into a world after WWIII where fighting, bombs, and radiation fallout cause the powers-that-be to clash and fight over control, secrets, technology, and more. In a land where the sun rarely touches the ground anymore, everything appears almost tainted and grey. Nothing is as it seems. Perceptions, emotions, and motives are always in question. A dangerous environment where a covert organization known as The Agency exists to control the rebel groups and revolts that threaten the government. With research, technology, manipulation, torture, and assassins, the Agency operates with brutal any-mean-necessary methods and force. And the best badass “guns blazing” assassin in the bunch is agent Hsin Vega (Sin).<br /><br /><b>”Sin’s gaze was intense; hawk-like. It was the glower of someone who could very easily reduce someone to a mass of shaking limbs if he chose.”</b> <br /><br />A killer simultaneously used, praised, shunned, and almost mythologized within the Agency for his skills and strength as a predator. Trained as a child by his father, violence is all Sin has known in life. Taught to kill and trust no one. Feared and punished even by the people that employ him, Sin is locked away in a box in an attempt to control his violent outbursts, snaps, and instability. If violence is all you have known though, how do you communicate or trust? Sin has been drugged and locked away for years, but a new plan and mission places Sin back in the field with a new partner. A partner to watch and control him. Boyd Beaulieu, a shattered, emotionless, introverted teenager is thrust into the job. I know what you must be thinking---Who in their right mind would suggest pairing a teenager with the agent known as the Monster? Well that would be Boyd’s mother! But don’t even get me started on Vivienne. I will let you meet that block of ice on your own! Can this new plan work? Can these two “social misfits” find a way to work together and not get each other killed? Somehow break out from their haunted pasts and perceptions people place on them? Maybe find what they need in each other to heal and survive? Haha…Shit! Now I sound like Boyd’s inner voice with all those questions. ;) I do know that Sin and Boyd reminded me how powerful, passionate and all-consuming the heat of intimacy, friendship and love can be.<br /><br /><b>”He could think of nothing but the intensity of the feelings coursing through him. The way this all felt, the sweaty, sliding heat of his skin and the hungry, muffled pants caught between their lips.”</b><br /><br /><br />The chemistry and energy captured on the page here was fucking mind-blowing! Like nothing I’ve experienced before in fiction! Intense, fierce, and insatiable. Sin’s green eyes captivated and caught me with one fiery look! When we first meet Boyd and Sin they are both so broken and haunted with such loneliness and vulnerability. The idea that one so strong, a killer, needed someone to protect him and reach out to him with kindness had my heart gulping for air! I don’t really want to spoil this experience with too many details—especially about Boyd’s past. Just know Boyd’s beautiful expressionless, guarded pout masks unbearable loss and fear. He broke my heart again and again. Boyd’s pain paired with Sin’s guarded sarcastic front and force formed a powerful “can’t look away” blend of emotion and tension. But wait! Just wait!<br /><br />To then witness their hearts slowly change! To see and feel the trust build over time by sharing pasts and space together was beautiful and addictive! Like Boyd, once I got a taste and look at their emotions—I wanted more! More! Their distinctive Sin &amp; Boyd brand of communicating with brutal honesty was hilarious, sad, and one of my favorite parts of their chemistry. I watched with bated breath as apathy changed to passion and curiosity changed to possessiveness. Hunger. Lust. Need. And Want! I’m ready to pop just thinking about it all now! Very, very sexy tension and heat that kept building and building! You will feel it in the air. My skin was flushed and shivering! The watching, flirting, denying, and touching that turned to such heat drove me crazy! God, I loved it all. <br /><br /><b>”Suddenly Sin’s taste was all around him; intoxicating and making him crave more. Every time he’d been attracted to Sin and had ignored it, every time he’d wondered what Sin would feel like pressed against him, came back at him in an overwhelming wave of desire.”</b><br /><br />There was something else living under the words as well though. A hard to explain energy and vibe that jumped off the page. A youthful, sometimes geeky and fun feeling mixed with a mesmerizing, voyeuristic intensity. A dark, dangerous pull that was sexy as all hell! Pure electric at times. Sparks of life, pain, and love that made me feel so alive! Evenfall is an exhilarating and exhausting read. One I will cherish as one of my favorites. <br /><br />My heart loved every step, miscommunication, flirty exchange, “Why?”, sweet craving, TOUCH, and silent moment shared between Sin and Boyd. Every moment seemed to burn into me. Sin’s lanky allure zinging across the page, Boyd’s mask slowly changing and cracking, and every rare ray of sunlight left a mark. What I wouldn’t do to be able to hear…<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ that first surprised, startled laugh float through the air. :D <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And just when I thought it couldn’t possibly get any hotter, the intensity any higher? Haha….Hell! The flash, feel, and taste of a lip ring shows up to completely bring me to my knees! :D <br /><br />Please. Dive in. Meet Sin and Boyd. Feel their touch. <br /><br /><br /><u>Extras:</u><br /><br />Ryan. My love! I’m putting you in my pocket for safe keeping. <br /><br />Carhart: The General piqued my curiosity at first sight. I’m watching you! *points finger*<br /><br /><u>Hsin: Sin, Sin, Sin!</u><br /><br />This is where Sin had me. Felt my heart squeeze right there and then.<br /><br />The breath on the window.<br /><br /><b>“he noticed Sin leaning in toward the passenger window, opening his mouth and breathing on it so fog curled against the glass….”<br /><br />“It was such a child-like thing for Sin to do that it distracted Boyd and he looked over. He never would have expected to see the man known as an psychopathic assassin do something a ten year old would do. The impression only grew when Sin reached up with one long finger and started drawing on the window.”</b> <br /><br />BAM! That was it. Just 7% in my heart knew it. I was in deep! <br /><br /><br /><u>Boyd. Oh Boyd!</u><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ You earned my full respect when you finally stood up to your mother. <br /><br />And damn if you didn’t knock my socks off with your “What kinda candy am I” flirty ways in Monterrey. Pure delicious and wicked! *grins* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br />Christina—Thank you once again. I know in my heart I would never have met Sin and Boyd without you. *bows and curtseys*<br /><br />Ilhem and all the ICoS gang—Thank you for the company and hand holding. I would be lost without you! :)<br /><br />Off for more…..<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11858876673395740303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15519959387996595156"><b>2.5 stars rounded up</b><br/><br/><br/><br/>I am <b>literally exhausted</b> after finishing this book tonight.<br/>I'll try not to write a long detailed review for it.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Let me start with the good news:</u>
</b><br/> <blockquote>
<br/>♥ It's worth to read it. It's worth it to victim your precious time for this book.<br/>♥ Boyd and HSin are amazing as a duo/team/friends/lovers. The chemistry between them is fantastic.<br/>♥ The storyline is not bad.<br/>♥ It could be fixed with a good editing. <br/>♥ My rating means nothing. You have to make your own reading experience. <br/>
</blockquote><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/35835594' rel='nofollow noopener'>My update</a></span>
  <span id="freeText15519959387996595156" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars rounded up</b><br><br><br><br>I am <b>literally exhausted</b> after finishing this book tonight.<br>I'll try not to write a long detailed review for it.<br><br><b>
  <u>Let me start with the good news:</u>
</b><br> <blockquote>
<br>♥ It's worth to read it. It's worth it to victim your precious time for this book.<br>♥ Boyd and HSin are amazing as a duo/team/friends/lovers. The chemistry between them is fantastic.<br>♥ The storyline is not bad.<br>♥ It could be fixed with a good editing. <br>♥ My rating means nothing. You have to make your own reading experience. <br>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/35835594" rel="nofollow noopener">My updates at 50%:</a><br><b>
  <u>My final conclusions:</u>
</b><br><blockquote>
<br>◆ IT IS NOT <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6708511-special-forces?from_search=true" rel="nofollow noopener">Special Forces</a>. NO WAY.<br>◆ Boyd and HSin, two great main characters that are worth discovering.<br>◆ The book is full of insignificant details, overloaded with the dialogs that are totally unimportant for the story. There are so many boring places and you'll find for sure some imprecision in the storytelling.<br>◆ A non-stop searching for a story itself that are buried sometimes under the mountains of words, phrases, sentences, pages IS TIRESOME! And exhausting. <br>◆ As it's a science fiction book I can't use the adjectives such as <i>unreal, illogical, ridiculous</i> and <i>incredible</i>. It is why I just say: <i>Agency, Missions, Briefings</i>.<br>◆ Sex scenes. They are good. But they are rare. I would like to replace a lot of fighting scenes that reminded me of a computer game with some hot intense sex scenes. Because the authors KNOW how to write them. <br>◆ The book needs urgently a good and strong editing. <br>◆ I'm not going to read the next sequel immediately after. But I want to read more of this authors.<br>◆ It's probably one of those MUST-READ-BOOKS, but I would recommend though to wait for an editing version. There are rumors that they are working on the editing. <br>◆ I overrate my stamina- I am not ready for the book 2 but I admire all my GR friends and all readers who read/are going to read all sequels at once. <br>
</blockquote><br><br><b>
  <i>If you read all reviews you'll notice that everybody wish a good and strong editing for this book. <u>I know that this editing requires the investment of a lot of time and much hard work. I don't expect it to be for free after and it is fair.</u> Every hard job should be rewarded. I just wish the authors do it though.<br></i>
</b> <br><br><b>

<span id="freeTextContainer3996698047812055468">This is my ideal kind of book; a real slow burner, with originality, a great concept and lots of angst. I am however, glad I had this week off work or it would have taken me a hell of a lot longer to get though it than just 8 days!<br/><br/>This is a dystopian post-war story about an unofficial government agency who are trying to infiltrate and bring down a rebel organisation. The two main characters Hsin and Boyd are newly appointed partners, who over a period of time, grow to trust and respect each othe</span>
  <span id="freeText3996698047812055468" style="display:none">This is my ideal kind of book; a real slow burner, with originality, a great concept and lots of angst. I am however, glad I had this week off work or it would have taken me a hell of a lot longer to get though it than just 8 days!<br /><br />This is a dystopian post-war story about an unofficial government agency who are trying to infiltrate and bring down a rebel organisation. The two main characters Hsin and Boyd are newly appointed partners, who over a period of time, grow to trust and respect each other, in the process forming an unconventional relationship. <br /><br />I felt the last part dragged a bit, but overall I absolutely loved this book and I am moving swiftly on to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8164593.Afterimage__In_the_Company_of_Shadows___2_" title="Afterimage (In the Company of Shadows, #2) by Sonny Hassell" rel="nofollow noopener">Afterimage</a>. Hoping there is a LOT more of Kassian in the next book!<br /><br />Just a couple of questions left unanswered:<br />Why is Owen always tired and needing coffee, what's he up to?<br />What exactly is wrong with Ryan?<br />After everything that's happened to Hsin, why is Carhart still fond of his father, Emilio?<br />Why did Hsin comment about his father saying "He knows....knew, where I am weak and he will exploit it, just like he did during my training" (is he still alive then?)<br />Following Hsin's torture, why does he now appear to have super human strength and amazing eyesight?</span>

<div id="review_310546431" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/310546431" />
    <a title="Lisa Arbitrary - AttentionIsArbitrary M/M Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7192208-lisa-arbitrary---attentionisarbitrary-m-m-blog"><img alt="Lisa Arbitrary - AttentionIsArbitrary M/M Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544994929p2/7192208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/310546431?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Arbitrary - AttentionIsArbitrary M/M Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Arbitrary - AttentionIsArbitrary M/M Blog" href="/user/show/7192208-lisa-arbitrary---attentionisarbitrary-m-m-blog">Lisa Arbitrary - AttentionIsArbitrary M/M Blog</a>

          added it

           <span class="uitext reviewText">m-m, gay, assassin, spy</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer310546431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8858258126843206451">**The following review reflects how I felt about the book at the time of reading. I do not believe in erasure, therefore I am letting my review stand.<br/><br/>However, due to too much supporting evidence of abuse, lies, fraud and slander, I can no longer recommend this work.<br/><br/><b>See: </b><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/164624031?order=a&page=1'>https://www.goodreads.com/user_status...</a><br/><br/>**<br/>~~~<br/><br/><b>Evenfall</b> is the first book in the In the Company of Shadows series. This free read is available at: <br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.aisylum.com/sonnyais/story.html#bk1'>http://www.aisylum.com/sonnyais/story...</a> <br/><br/>I think I'm friends with some of the cooles</span>
  <span id="freeText8858258126843206451" style="display:none">**The following review reflects how I felt about the book at the time of reading. I do not believe in erasure, therefore I am letting my review stand.<br><br>However, due to too much supporting evidence of abuse, lies, fraud and slander, I can no longer recommend this work.<br><br><b>See: </b><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/164624031?order=a&amp;page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/user_status...</a><br><br>**<br>~~~<br><br><b>Evenfall</b> is the first book in the In the Company of Shadows series. This free read is available at: <br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.aisylum.com/sonnyais/story.html#bk1">http://www.aisylum.com/sonnyais/story...</a> <br><br>I think I'm friends with some of the coolest people on Goodreads, in my opinion, and for as long as I can remember they've been talking about this thing called ICoS and Evenfall. These discussions often include references to Hsin, the Agency, Monsters and Sonny and Ais. What? I was starting to think it was a cult following more than a book to be read. Heh, funny how I was so close to the truth. Just go check out the author's website, you'll see what I mean. These fans are serious. Even though this is a free read, I'm quite <i>invested.</i><br><br><br><b>
  <u>THE STORY</u>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>"How much desolation was there in the world today, how much more now than had been even two decades ago before that first bomb exploded on foreign soil?"</i>
</b><br><br>In post-WWIII America the world is frighteningly familiar. <i>The Agency</i> is secretly in charge of containing threats from terrorists and other rebel groups. Within this covert operation we meet Hsin, a level-10 field agent who is like no other. Boyd is a very broken boy, who's had a rough time of emotionally coping with reality. Hsin is VERY real. These two are thrust together in ridiculously dangerous situations. Despite the internal struggles, risky objectives and lack of common ground, there are sexy glances, quirky lips, tattoos, calloused hands and solid, sinuous muscle groups. Oh right, the story. So "Sin" and Boyd begin to grow on one another while we learn more about the Agency and their objectives around the world. Their assignments are made much more difficult because of their complete lack of social skills. So, what we want to know is; Can two social losers find love?<br><br><b>
  <i>"No thanks, sweetheart. That brief moment of insanity has passed."</i>
</b><br><br>The storyline is solid and multifaceted unfortunately it could have been told in half the time. See, The Writing, below.<br><br><i>
  <b>After all, a life without living was simply a death without dying."</b>
</i><br><br><b>
  <u>THE CHARACTERS</u>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>"He is valuable material to the Agency"</i>
</b><br><br>Hsin Liu Vega is considered a deadly monster. Though <i>he</i> has been isolated and tortured, he is generally hated, feared and loathed but not without reason. On the surface, it should be Sin who has me in knots since I love the sexy, dangerous, brooding, cryptic types. Unfortunately, there isn't enough of Sin's POV throughout this book to clinch the deal. Don't get me wrong, he is fascinating and damn sexy, I guess I just need more Sin.<br><br><b>
  <i>"Would anyone remember that he'd ever lived?"</i>
</b><br><br>Boyd Beaulieu on the other hand, <i>is</i> in the story so much you could easily forget that there are other characters. I've never met such a long-winded, endlessly pondering character - Ever. I like Boyd. He's delightfully bland, an emotional void and arousingly androgenous. I really like Boyd but he needed to turn off for a while. Through his epically long internal dialogs, I feel like I know Boyd completely. I just know him about ten times over, that's all. <br><br>Conners - Asshole.<br>Carhart - Diggin' him.<br>Vivienne - Bitch, but mysteriously so.<br>Lou - The boyfriend.<br>Ryan - Geek extraordinaire. <br>Owen - ??? Hm?<br>Jeffrey - Arrogant <br>Thierry - The player.<br><br><b>
  <i>"Who are you interested in, then? Men? Women?" "I've grown to despise both."</i>
</b><br><br>I really like, love and care about the characters. That's the hook for me in this book. If the characters hadn't held my interest like they did, I may not have been able to slog through the sloggy parts. See, The Writing, below.<br><br><br><b>
  <u>THE WRITING</u>
</b><br><br>Note 1 on my Kindle is: This reads a bit like the elementary readers, Dick and Jane. That's harsh and certainly doesn't hold true for long, it's just that I was trying to capture how choppy it felt. Like I said, that didn't last. Instead it turned into the longest winded read of my life. It started to read much like a loosely edited fanfic. Most often points of the narrative were repeated multiple times and while that drove the point home it just drove me crazy. As I said, I liked the story and the characters so I really feel like this book could gain a lot from some strong, very strong editing. <br><br>I have to say that there were also many moments that reached me and caused solid emotional responses. Everything from laugh out loud moments to seriously heart-wrenching drama, to <i>"wow, I finally just took a breath"</i> moments are written into this book. The authors have the skills and know how, they just need the discipline to pare it down.<br><br>"A few minutes passed before he reemerged in a dark green t-shirt with a picture of a pinwheel on it and white letters beneath that said simply, 'Blow me.'"<br><br>~~~<br><br><b>Take a look at my Male/Male Romance Book Blog:</b> <br><br><a href="http://www.attentionisarbitrary.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379800439i/669513._SX540_.png" width="310" height="133" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>http://www.attentionisarbitrary.blogspot.com </a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8858258126843206451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText9381549085837939884" style="display:none"><br />I really have no idea how I'm ever going to review this.. <br /><br />First of all, I feel like I've been reading this story/book for the last 8 weeks.. Its an online story of 45 chapters and an epilogue, but there are no page numbers, so I have no idea how long it is, or how much I've actually read in the last couple of days.. But.. its a lot!<br /><br />Can I just say, before I go into whats its about, that:<br /><br /><i>Holy Mother of sweet baby Jesus!!</i><br /><br />This is good.. This is soooooo goood!! *growls*<br /><br />Ok, now that I got that out of my system, I can go on..<br /><br />I feel like this is a mix of the Special Forces books, and the Administration books.. <br /><br />Its about Boyd and Sin. Sin has been trained to be a killer since he was 8. His dad was a big-ass assassin, and trained his son to be the same. And with Sin's whole background, its not a surprise that he turns out to be a monster, who can kill anyone and everyone in the blink of an eye.. Sin has a lot of problems. Mentally and.. yeah well.. A lot of problems. When we meet him, he's been locked in a tiny cage for 6 months, and when his only weakness is claustrophobia, yeah, he's not in his happy place..<br /><br />In comes Boyd. He's been picked to be Sin's new partner. Let me say that this story is taking place in the nearest future, after a WWIII situation. Sin works for <i>The Agency</i>. Anywho.. In comes Boyd as Sin's new partner. And when you think about Sin killing his last 4 partners.. yeah.. Boyd doesnt have high hopes for how this is going to turn out.. <br /><br />But Boyd is the first person to see something else in Sin, other than him being a monster and therefore a friendship forms..<br /><br />This is about Sin finding out that life can be something else than just killing, and he discovers that he is actually capable of trusting another person.. <br /><br />Ok, this is a very rough draft.. And there is sooo much going on. Missions, fights, killing, whatever.. <br /><br />Let me just say that this is without a doubt the longest bulid-up to a "first kiss" I've read.. Holy hell!!<br /><br />But when it happened?? <i>Jesus Christ!</i><br /><br />Soooo goood!!! This is just.. So. Freaking. Good.<br /><br />There were whole chapters of me wildly shivering <s>and moaning</s>, because everything they said to eachother was just <b>that</b> good, and everything they did to eachother was just <b>that</b> good, and everything was just <b>that</b> fucking good! There were so many one-liners that had me shivering in this book, that its just insane actually! <br /><br />Sin... Mmmmm.. I love him! I freaking love this dude! With everything from his freaky green eyes to how he responded to Boyd.. Grrrr! <br /><br /><i>"I want whatever you want to give me."</i><br /><br />Give him everything, Boyd!!! Please dear God, give him everything he wants!<br /><br />I absolutly LOVED this story, and I cannot wait to start the 2nd.. Which I will, about 2 seconds after I'm done here.. </span>

<div id="review_145558027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145558027" />
    <a title="Mel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2295424-mel"><img alt="Mel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305638929p2/2295424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145558027?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel" href="/user/show/2295424-mel">Mel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2295424-mel?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2295424-mel?shelf=fan-freakin-tastic">fan-freakin-tastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2295424-mel?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2295424-mel?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2295424-mel?shelf=free-stuff">free-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2295424-mel?shelf=on-line-fiction">on-line-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145558027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16877442825917915112">I started reading this story because of the manic raving of my trusted Goodreads friends. They promised a highly addictive and emotional roller coaster ride which spread over four books and thousands of pages. Safe to say I immediately made the connection to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6708511.Special_Forces' title='Special Forces by Aleksandr Voinov' rel='nofollow noopener'>Special Forces</a> and had very high expectations.<br/><br/><i>Evenfall</i> was totally different than I had expected. Unlike that other epic m/m book, I didn’t have a constant sense of panic while reading, which meant that this time around I wasn't forsaking sl</span>
  <span id="freeText16877442825917915112" style="display:none">I started reading this story because of the manic raving of my trusted Goodreads friends. They promised a highly addictive and emotional roller coaster ride which spread over four books and thousands of pages. Safe to say I immediately made the connection to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6708511.Special_Forces" title="Special Forces by Aleksandr Voinov" rel="nofollow noopener">Special Forces</a> and had very high expectations.<br /><br /><i>Evenfall</i> was totally different than I had expected. Unlike that other epic m/m book, I didn’t have a constant sense of panic while reading, which meant that this time around I wasn't forsaking sleep and food just in order to read a few pages more. A lot of parts were too fantastical, lacked nuance and not to mention good common sense. There was too much introspection which was repetitive and at times slowed the story down and towards the ending the story just seemed to be going on and on.<br /><br />This all being said: I liked the book. A lot. Dystopia, government conspiracies, prejudices, parental issues, identity problems, m/m lovin’; you name it: the book had it. And -despite the absurdity of some situations and the overabundance of internal monologues- the events and psychological consequences were dealt with in a very satisfying manner. The tension was built up gradually, the action had me on the edge of my seat and the love scenes had me fanning myself. <br /><br />I found Sin and Boyd to be wonderfully captivating and as the book progressed they got more and more layered. I loved how these two seemingly polar opposites turned out to be much more alike than one would have thought and how their relationship lead to learning from each other and about themselves. <br /><br />All in all <i>Evenfall</i> was a great book (4,5 stars) and I'm very curious about the sequel. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16877442825917915112" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2930102566174407488"><i>Bruh</i><br/><br/>I did it. There were times where I was going to quit and DNF it in the middle, but because of all the amazing 4/5 stars rating, I pushed through. <br/><br/>And at long last, I finished. <br/><br/>The overall plot was good, although I do wish that I didn't have to shift</span>
  <span id="freeText2930102566174407488" style="display:none"><i>Bruh</i><br><br>I did it. I fucking did it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1540736700ra/26512303.gif" width="450" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>1200 pages, and after hundreds of hours trying to get through this book, the bitch finally did it. <br><br>At first I was skeptical, because shit, I ain't gonna be wasting my time reading over thousand of pages just for a mediocre book. There were times where I was going to quit and DNF it in the middle, but because of all the amazing 4/5 stars rating, I pushed through. <br><br>And at long last, I finished. <br><br>The overall plot was good, although I do wish that I didn't have to shift through so much <i>words and gibberish</i> just to get to the meat of the story. There just seems to be so much redundant words of pages upon pages of describing their surroundings, their mission, the sky. Like shit, it's fine if you do it every now and then, but doing it every single time was really unnecessary. <br><br>And as most people say, this book needs a good editor because the plot was pretty okay, there were plot holes here and there, a lot of things that happened in this book could be better capitalized, but we're not gonna go into that as I'm keeping out hope that it will improve in the second book. The writing, though, could really do with some cleaning up. <br><br>Like cut it to half it's length type of cleaning up. <br><br>But since there was already a shortened version of this book, and yes, I did choose to read the longer version of it, I won't go too much into details about the editing as I am sure the newer version are very much improved.<br><br>The sole reason why I even decided to keep pushing through until the end was mainly, and honestly because of Sin and Boyd. Needless to say, I love these two. Especially Sin, that man with his sweet-tooth and sometimes childish tendencies will be the death of me I swear. <br><br>Other than that, not much to complain about. Now, please do pray for my sanity as I continue down book 2 that also seems to be 1000 pages long.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459947072ra/18676918.gif" width="450" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Blog : <a href="http://literaturesandmovies.com" rel="nofollow noopener">More of me in writing form</a><br><br>Youtube : <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCeEAFz7timmDVbph_Mgox6Q" rel="nofollow noopener">le youchube here</a><br><br>IG : <a href="http://instagram.com/caterpillarbuddies/" rel="nofollow noopener">and instagram here</a></b></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer721370751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13152833219725752347"> <s>I will write my review as soon as I organize my thoughts...</s><br/><br/>Evenfall is a fabulous book and left me exhausted. It is so long… I would give 5 stars if it had not so many boring and annoying parts. In the beginning I thought that so detailed descriptions and dialogues had a meaning, but, as the reading went by, I realized that it is the writing style… and so, all those boring parts were irrelevant and unnecessary, and the book would be shorter and less tiring without them.<br/><br/>Nevertheless, the story i</span>
  <span id="freeText13152833219725752347" style="display:none"> <s>I will write my review as soon as I organize my thoughts...</s><br><br>Evenfall is a fabulous book and left me exhausted. It is so long… I would give 5 stars if it had not so many boring and annoying parts. In the beginning I thought that so detailed descriptions and dialogues had a meaning, but, as the reading went by, I realized that it is the writing style… and so, all those boring parts were irrelevant and unnecessary, and the book would be shorter and less tiring without them.<br><br>Nevertheless, the story itself shows two amazing and creative minds, and the characters that these authors created are absolutely rich, complex and absorbents!!! Some of these characters I really liked… others I really hated.<br><br>The MC characters however, marked this book in an unforgettable way.<br><br><b>Boyd</b><br><br><a href="http://s1296.photobucket.com/user/igrilo/media/452092_zps36391661.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385980111i/7268725.jpg" alt=" photo 452092_zps36391661.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Boyd is a vulnerable and broken young man without a reason to live.<br><br>“After all, a life without living was simply a death without dying.”<br><br>He made some mistakes that made very angry with him. However he grows and became more confident and trustworthy. In this amazing plot, he meets the man that will give him all the motives to fight for his happiness and for his life. <br><br>He meets his partner who became is best friend and his lover:<br><br><b>Hsin!!!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1296.photobucket.com/user/igrilo/media/cortada2_zps80a421cd.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1385980111i/7268726.jpg" alt=" photo cortada2_zps80a421cd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>I don't know how to even start to say what I feel about Hsin/Sin… First I have to say that he is on my top 5 list of the best male characters ever!!! <br><br>“ 'So many and so various laws are giv’n; So many laws argue so many sins'”<br><br>I love him! I love his beauty, his green eyes, his arrogance and sarcasm, I love his strength and intelligence, I love his vulnerability and even the way he loves Boyd!<br><br>He is perfect and magnificent!!!<br><br>I will never forget him, and I will continue to read this series mostly because of him!<br><br>Hsin and Boyd share some of the greatest, hottest and overwhelming scenes that I ever read… The talking, the teasing, the looks, the kisses, the sex… what a turn on scenes!<br><br><a href="http://s1296.photobucket.com/user/igrilo/media/tumblr_mqh7moD7YZ1qjzwvbo2_250_zps2bd7e47b.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385980111ra/7268727.gif" width="600" alt=" photo tumblr_mqh7moD7YZ1qjzwvbo2_250_zps2bd7e47b.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1507202883" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1507202883" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1507202883?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1507202883" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6484546829382094887">This is one of those books where I have an internal argument with myself on how to rate it. <br/><br/>Right Brain: I need to give it all the stars because I'm in love with the characters and the story is awesome.<br/><br/>Left Brain: No, you romantic fool, you need to give it a low star rating because you know this book needed some serious editing.<br/><br/>Right Brain: You are so anal retentive! You know it's the feels that matter.<br/><br/>Left Brain: Feelings are for fools. My mathematical calculations say that this book could have</span>
  <span id="freeText6484546829382094887" style="display:none">This is one of those books where I have an internal argument with myself on how to rate it. <br><br>Right Brain: I need to give it all the stars because I'm in love with the characters and the story is awesome.<br><br>Left Brain: No, you romantic fool, you need to give it a low star rating because you know this book needed some serious editing.<br><br>Right Brain: You are so anal retentive! You know it's the feels that matter.<br><br>Left Brain: Feelings are for fools. My mathematical calculations say that this book could have been at least 100 pages shorter.<br><br>Right Brain: <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453886670i/17884494.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, we all know who won. My pretty pretty pony side.<br><br>This book is about Sin and Boyd who work as special agents for a government agency that squashes any form of rebellion by killing everyone. Works for me. Kill em all, let God sort them out.<br><br>Anyway, we start our story with Boyd, who is described as being young (only 18), man-pretty with long blonde hair, androgynous looks, and thin. Here's my Boyd:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453886670i/17884495.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Boyd is brought in as a new partner for Sin, who has killed all of his previous partners. They are hoping his personality will blend better with Sin, and maybe he will live longer than a month. Sin is known as the "monster", and has been an assassin since he was 14. He is now 28 and has killed more people than your average serial killer. And, with less remorse. Sin is described as dark haired with very green eyes and olive skin. Here's my Sin:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453886670i/17884496._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The thing is, Sin has been misjudged and beaten down pretty badly. He has absolutely no social skills because he has been punished and kept in a cell or box most of his life, and he trusts nobody. Because of his reputation, the people at the agency are all terrified of Sin and hurry away from him at sight. They think he is a rabid, evil dog that needs to be put down. But, Boyd has been depressed and suicidal for the last couple of years. He was given records on Sin, but sees the truth that Sin has been mistreated by the agency. Because of his thoughts about this mistreatment, and his lack of caring if he dies anyway, he has no fear of Sin. This totally freaks Sin out.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453886671i/17884497.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, Boyd is the first person to ever treat Sin like a human being and Sin ends up deciding that it would be best if Boyd doesn't die. That's practically an "I love you" in human terms. <br><br>Thus begins the amazing partnership that eventually turns into a romance. And, when I say "eventually", I mean so slowly that you feel like you want to shoot someone. Seriously, this is a long book, so that romance doesn't happen for 600 frustrating pages! I just wanted to:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453886671i/17884498._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Come on already!!!<br><br>Along with the romance that developed slower than my rush to get the latest Justin Beiber cd, we get the story of their missions - which are pretty interesting. There is a lot of action, killing, betrayal, torture, and explosions. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442417234ra/16232007.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As I've mentioned - this book is long. Like War &amp; Peace long. But, because of that we really get to know the characters. Even the side characters are well-developed. And, the action scenes are well-written. You can visualize everything going on. It gets really complicated, but the story is really engrossing and easy to follow. I loved Sin &amp; Boyd, and I loved Ryan &amp; Carhart, and I'm really intrigued with Boyd's mother. I'm glad this is a series because I can't wait to find out what happens next. (That's right, it was over 1,000 pages and yet the story isn't over! ;-))</span>
  <a data-text-id="6484546829382094887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_221894127" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221894127" />
    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5171122-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351356033p2/5171122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/221894127?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/5171122-christina">Christina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5171122-christina?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5171122-christina?shelf=free">free</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5171122-christina?shelf=m-m-romance">m-m-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5171122-christina?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5171122-christina?shelf=military">military</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer221894127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7489334246207410884">***Possible Spoilers<br/><br/><br/><br/>Whew, where to begin with this one. I guess I'll start with Sin. Sexy, Sexy, Sexy! I don't have enough words to describe how incredibly HOT he is. Here's what Boyd sees when he first encounters Sin: over six feet tall, jet black hair, think long black eyelashes, vivid green eyes, sculptured full lips, high cheekbones, caramel-tinted tan complexion, thin body crafted entirely into muscle, moves like a predator. And this isn't even the half of it. <br/> <br/>Ok, ok, onto the story. <br/> <br/>Even</span>
  <span id="freeText7489334246207410884" style="display:none">***Possible Spoilers<br /><br /><br /><br />Whew, where to begin with this one. I guess I'll start with Sin. Sexy, Sexy, Sexy! I don't have enough words to describe how incredibly HOT he is. Here's what Boyd sees when he first encounters Sin: over six feet tall, jet black hair, think long black eyelashes, vivid green eyes, sculptured full lips, high cheekbones, caramel-tinted tan complexion, thin body crafted entirely into muscle, moves like a predator. And this isn't even the half of it. <br /> <br />Ok, ok, onto the story. <br /> <br />Evenfall takes place in a dystopian future after WWIII. Hsin Liu Vega (Sin) is one of the top agents working in a secret division of the government that deals with anti-war/government groups. Sin was trained by his father at the age of eight to become an assassin. He is the best at what he does, however he is also mentally unstable and kills at the drop of a hat. Because of this he is labeled "The Monster". Well, it's no wonder since he was trained to become a killer from the time he was a young boy. Then there are the many other disturbing facts that come out about his childhood and all the cruel and sadistic "punishments" inflicted repeatedly on him by The Agency for his disobedience. They isolate him and mentally and physically torment him. They keep him in a locked box knowing he's claustrophobic and in order to control him, they use a neck collar which emits electric shocks when activated. My poor Sin :(<br /><br />Anyway, Sin is needed on an extremely important mission but needs a partner to keep him under control. Of course it's difficult to find someone since Sin doesn't get along with anyone and has played a role in the death of his last 4 partners. Now, here comes Boyd!<br /><br />Boyd Beaulieu, is the introverted son of one of the top officials in The Agency and is recommended for the job. Boyd is the first person not to judge Sin and wants to genuinely work with him. However, Boyd also comes with his own set of emotional baggage. They both begin to realize that they are more alike than they think. They slowly break down each other's walls and begin to trust each ane other. They are also incredibly attracted to one another. The build-up is slow but their chemistry together is crazy good and when they finally do get together, Holy Hell it's scorching! I had a hard time breathing when these two got together.<br /><br />This book has a lot going on. There's the government missions and intrigue, Sin and Boyd's internal battles, their growing relationship, their past relationships, their relationships with family and colleagues and all this comes together in an amazing story. Without realizing it, Sin and Boyd open up new sides to each other which neither of them knew existed.<br /><br />What prevented this from being a 5-star is how wordy and repetitive it is. This drags down the book tremendously. Not only was the content repetitive but I also noticed the same phrases used several times. Boyd's over-analytical and endless inner monologue's were extremely difficult to get through. It just went on and on and sometimes over ridicules things, like how Boyd was going to work an oven. I mean, we really didn't need him analyzing the in and outs of an oven. But I guess that's Boyd. Besides this, I also found myself questioning some of the logic of the decisions that Sin and Boyd made on missions. <br />There were also scenes that were very unrealistic. I love Sin but it's a bit unbelievable that he can take on a room of 30 armed men and come out of it alive. <br /> <br />One of the most memorable lines that touched me was when Sin was looking at the painting called Atonement. It was a depiction of a boy standing alone in a bombed out city after the war. He was in uniform, covered in dirt and blood and had an empty stare. Sin saw himself. He says the boy, the soldier needed to atone for his actions in the war, for the lives he took and possibly look for a way to make up for what he's done. What I loved was the artist's interpretation. She stated: <i> "Perhaps it is not him who is in need of atonement. Maybe it is....the world. The world, the powers that be....they created a generation of soldiers like him. Boy fighters, child killers, ones who did not have the chance to live before the world armed them and so, they had no idea how to live when the fighting was no longer needed." </i> <br />Sin indentified with the boy and I guess it was this moment that Sin's pain became so overwhelming to me. <br /><br />Despite the issues I mentioned above, I loved this book. Sin and Boyd make it all worth it. I loved the plot, the action kept me on the edge of my seat and I can't wait for more. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7489334246207410884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_392143805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/392143805" />
    <a title="Vivian ♪(┌・。・)┌		" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6068010-vivian"><img alt="Vivian ♪(┌・。・)┌		" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455434027p2/6068010.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/392143805?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivian ♪(┌・。・)┌		" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivian ♪(┌・。・)┌		" href="/user/show/6068010-vivian">Vivian ♪(┌・。・)┌		</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6068010-vivian?shelf=fire-to-the-sheets">fire-to-the-sheets</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6068010-vivian?shelf=gaymance">gaymance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6068010-vivian?shelf=holy-fucking-swoon">holy-fucking-swoon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6068010-vivian?shelf=adored">adored</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6068010-vivian?shelf=gritty">gritty</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer392143805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13459738371638792461">I have this book now... But I'm not gonna to touch till my HEA is confirmed. If not, I'm afraid I will have to abandon this ship. :(<br/><br/><b>pre-reading review</b><br/><br/>--------------------------<br/><br/>Hah, how ignorant I was back then...<br/><br/>I really want to write a fantastical review that can illustrate, communicate and summarise everything I felt about this book, but I suppose I've come across a mental block. Or maybe it's just one of the few books where I can't think of anything to write about except how frustrating it is</span>
  <span id="freeText13459738371638792461" style="display:none">I have this book now... But I'm not gonna to touch till my HEA is confirmed. If not, I'm afraid I will have to abandon this ship. :(<br /><br /><b>pre-reading review</b><br /><br />--------------------------<br /><br />Hah, how ignorant I was back then...<br /><br />I really want to write a fantastical review that can illustrate, communicate and summarise everything I felt about this book, but I suppose I've come across a mental block. Or maybe it's just one of the few books where I can't think of anything to write about except how frustrating it is that I can't think of anything to write about. Here's to trying.<br /><br />As much as I hate this cliche metaphor, this book was a <i>rollercoaster</i>. One long-ass, emotionally and mentally taxing ride filled to the brim with a disgustingly long list of emotions and feels: boredom, curiosity, interest, excitement, amusement, adoration, lust, adoration, lust, adoration... I'm pretty sure you can spot where Mexico is. *snort* I'm finally one of <i>them</i>. The fangirls who throw the word "Mexico" around with knowing glee. I'm finally in on the secret.<br /><br />To an <i>outsider</i> (glee), one of perhaps the greatest mysteries is how this book can elicit such strong emotions and bone deep loyalty from readers, even as they throw around words like "repetitive" or phrases like "meaningless detail". Such contradictions isn't really one you can explain. To explain is to just blurt out all of these gruesome feels and frantic, jumbled words that may or may not sound like "Sin"... "Mexico"... "Sin"... "Boyd"... "sinboydsex"..."Boyd"... I'll admit. I loved Boyd and Sin. Together. Together they were literally magic. I just-- *speechless emotionally crying feels*<br /><br />Anyway. I'll try not to sound like a broken record echoing every other reviewer (and saying it much less eloquently) but this was <b>fucking long</b>. But interestingly enough, once I was actually dragged into the story (more like I was tossed into it head first) I didn't find myself caring about the length all too much. I noted how long it took to progress to the next percent, but I really did enjoy nearly all of it. <br /><br />The writing isn't the most colourful I've seen, but it was well crafted and very skilfully painted the story inside my head, managing to provoke extremely visceral reactions from me and set my heart alight (among other things). The sex scenes... *fades into black before I embarrass myself*<br /><br />Another problem I had was the occasional inconsistencies I spotted and also the plausibility of some scenarios. I'm not a stickler for such details and I mostly don't even notice them, but it is always nice to have everything line up together. And though I cannot claim to have lived in a dystopian society and lived the high life of an assassin or anything of that sort, but some things just don't <i>seem right</i>, and I do take note of that, even if it doesn't detract from my enjoyment of the novel.<br /><br />Overall? <i>Evenfall</i> can be described by a whole range of negative adjectives which have been mentioned by a hundred different reviewers; however, at the end of the day, it can also (and is usually) summed up with only four words: <b>I fucking loved it</b>.<br /><br />Rating: 4.25 give or take</span>
  <a data-text-id="13459738371638792461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14992704918010943092" style="display:none">I'm removing my rating, but not my review. I still love this series, even though I most definitely do not condone what SH has done. <br><br>-------------------------------------------<br><br>I can hardly explain how I feel about this book. Perhaps I should describe my life the past week while reading this book. I am soooooooo tired.... because I haven't had much sleep. I read while I was cooking, I read while I was cleaning the toilet (that was a challenge), I got up early in the morning to just keep reading and I read while I should have been sleeping (sleep is so overrated)... Yes it was that good!<br><br>I fell in love with Hsin (Sin) from the first page. He was so badass yet sweet. The perfect combination. He absolutely did not care what people thought of him. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380393578i/757763._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And Boyd, my Boyd. I cannot express my love for him with simple words. The way he had given up on life and was trying to be emotionless, I was so intrigued. Because as it turns out, he was such an incredibly passionate person. He did everything with such conviction.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1408995251i/10918973._SY540_.jpg" width="280" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And when these two got together. OMG, explosion! The sex scenes, wow! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491693931ra/22437456.gif" width="380" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And the world building, just awesome. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1408995251i/10918974._SX540_.jpg" width="380" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sin and Boy are my favorite couple of all time. Their chemistry together was amazing.<br><br>Highly recommended.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fN+H/yE+yDsPkwL1av+kW440hEFGP66QjT/g+8r/Epeb096isf/ILHrdTPiz98cUrcLy+tE22uu9660JL/3RAA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Mwj7sK5Zao6qbo175zPO65ZYLPZZMik6RcrVkwz96T7UBKLtPphqmd8gw3Y+O62kta5aTc47XUF1Hphh6f8qqQ==')})
  }
